From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct  2 14:11:14 2001

Subject: [Xitami] Xitame CGI Linux
Message-ID: <0110021002.AA1002028369@germanlloyd.org>

Hi,

I think you'll have to modify the first line of your cgi-scripts.
On Windows-System it will be something like #!c:\perl\bin\perl.exe,
or wherever you instllalled Perl.
On most Unix-Systems Perl will be found at /usr/local/bin/ , so change
that line to #!/usr/local/bin/perl .

Regards, Axel Dahlke

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct  2 16:55:51 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 02 Oct 2001 11:55:51 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitame CGI Linux
References: <3BB9AC8F.75B5E038@knoop.nl>
Message-ID: <3BB9E387.7D8A0934@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Linux server ... unable to execute Perl CGI scripts.

Does it have Perl? 

Where is it? 

What is the first line of your scripts? 

The first line of Perl scripts to run on Xitami cross-platform must be 

#! /usr/local/bin/perl

Or whatever the exact path to the Perl program is. 

With Xitami there is no need to change that line for Windows. Even
though Windows rarely has a /usr/local/bin. If the #! line has "perl" at
the end, and the directory does not exist, Windows Xitami will search on
PATH to find Perl. 

 -PRR

In-Reply-To: <F166jvM9KfYDovvQ0Pu00004180@hotmail.com>

Hello.
One possible solution of user rights at NT is running Xitami as a service
logged as defined account.
You can set the account under which will be Xitami running
in Settings/Services/Startup... - Log on as ...
Use existing account or create new one especially for Xitami and
set the permisions on files as you like for that account.
Used account have to be allowed to "Log on as a servrice"
in Administrative tools/User manager for domains/Policies/User rights/
then check the box "Advanced user rights", find "Log on as service"
and add an "user".
This works very nice for me as I need to have cgi scripts running under
"normal" user account to be able to access database server.
                                         Bye
                                                 Zdenko Rohac.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct  4 01:03:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 04 Oct 2001 12:03:32 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] FTP-passive mode
In-Reply-To: Message from Andreas Zieritz <zieritz@sovik.no>
 of "Wed, 03 Oct 2001 15:01:06 +0200." <3BBB0C12.FC98DF56@sovik.no>
Message-ID: <200110040003.MAA22370@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3BBB0C12.FC98DF56@sovik.no>, Andreas Zieritz writes:
>We have moved our Xitami Webserver behind a firewall (see
>www.smoothwall.org) and we do have some troubles with the FTP part. What
>we have found out is that some FTP clients do have a problem in
>establishing a communication with the Xitami server. FTP-clients
>operating in passive mode are not experiencing these problems.
>We have opened ports 20 and 21 on the firewall. Are there any other
>ports that should be open?  Any hints concerning passive mode?

I'm a little puzzled as to what your problem is; you say "FTP-clients
operating in pasive mode are not experiencing these problems", but also
say "Any hints concerning passive mode?".

The FTP protocol is _really_ not designed to go through firewalls (it
was designed well before anyone had even thought of the need for
firewalls, let alone actually designed a firewall).  You should probably
seriously consider whether you can do what you want with HTTP instead of
FTP.

If you still want to use FTP you need to remember that there are two
modes of FTP:
1. Active FTP:  control connection open from client->server; if the client
   wants to download something, the client picks a port number at its,
   end and the server connects to that port, and sends the file.  If the
   client wants to upload something the server picks a port number at
   its end, and the client connects to that.  (Ie, the connection for
   transfering the data always opens in the connection the data is being
   sent.)

2. Passive FTP: control connection open from client->server; if the
   client wants to download something the server picks a port number at
   its end, and tells the client to connect there to "pull" the file
   back.  If the client wants to upload something the server picks a
   port number at its end, and the client connects to that.  (Ie, the
   connection for transfering data is always opened from the client to
   the server.)

Using passive mode usually gets around most problems with firewalls at
the _client_ end.  But it causes complications if there is also a
firewall at the _server_ end.

There are two basic complications caused by passive FTP when the server
is behind a firewall:
1. The port that is picked by the FTP server may not be allowed through
   the firewall.  Since the FTP server needs to allow more than one
   connection at a time, this may mean multiple ports need to be allowed
   through the firewall.

2. If the firewall is doing NAT, the address given out to connect to by 
   the FTP server will probaly be an internal address, not an external
   one, and thus not usable.

The main complication caused by active FTP is at the client end, where
their firewall may not allow an incoming connection to whatever port the
client picks; but many firewalls can handle this automatically.

Debugging this sort of thing generally requires snooping on the TCP/IP
traffic at one or both ends, and figuring out what each end is trying to
do.

Generally it's all too hard; and if you're going to have your server
behind a firewall you probably want to avoid using FTP.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

   sent.)

2. Passive FTP: control connection open from client->server; if the
   client wants to download something the server picks a port number at
   its end, and tells the client to connect there to "pull" the file
   back.  If the client wants to upload something the server picks a
   port number at its end, and the client connects to that.  (Ie, the
   connection for transfering data is always opened from the client to
   the server.)

Using passive mode usually gets around most problems with firewalls at
the _client_ end.  But it causes complications if there is also a
firewall at the _server_ end.

There are two basic complications caused by passive FTP when the server
is behind a firewall:
1. The port that is picked by the FTP server may not be allowed through
   the firewall.  Since the FTP server needs to allow more than one
   connection at a time, this may mean multiple ports need to be allowed
   through the firewall.

2. If the firewall is doing NAT, the address given out to connect to by 
   the FTP server will probaly be an internal address, not an external
   one, and thus not usable.

The main complication caused by active FTP is at the client end, where
their firewall may not allow an incoming connection to whatever port the
client picks; but many firewalls can handle this automatically.

Debugging this sort of thing generally requires snooping on the TCP/IP
traffic at one or both ends, and figuring out what each end is trying to
do.

Generally it's all too hard; and if you're going to have your server
behind a firewall you probably want to avoid using FTP.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

> The FTP protocol is _really_ not designed to go through firewalls (it

>    end and the server connects to that port, and sends the file.  If the
>    client wants to upload something the server picks a port number at
>    its end, and the client connects to that.  (Ie, the connection for
>    transfering the data always opens in the connection the data is being
>    sent.)

>    client wants to download something the server picks a port number at
>    its end, and tells the client to connect there to "pull" the file
>    back.  If the client wants to upload something the server picks a
>    port number at its end, and the client connects to that.  (Ie, the
>    connection for transfering data is always opened from the client to
>    the server.)
>
> Using passive mode usually gets around most problems with firewalls at
> the _client_ end.  But it causes complications if there is also a
> firewall at the _server_ end.
>
> There are two basic complications caused by passive FTP when the server
> is behind a firewall:
> 1. The port that is picked by the FTP server may not be allowed through
>    the firewall.  Since the FTP server needs to allow more than one
>    connection at a time, this may mean multiple ports need to be allowed
>    through the firewall.
>
> 2. If the firewall is doing NAT, the address given out to connect to by
>    the FTP server will probaly be an internal address, not an external
>    one, and thus not usable.
>
> The main complication caused by active FTP is at the client end, where
> their firewall may not allow an incoming connection to whatever port the
> client picks; but many firewalls can handle this automatically.

Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 14:46:28 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] 'ddnsdef.xml' is not readable
In-Reply-To: Message from Melle.koning@endemol.nl
 of "Tue, 18 Sep 2001 10:42:53 +0200." <5B983AB5F20BD511A3EE0002A52C3CB6E6D6F0@JDM_EXCHANGE.hilversum.endemol.com>
Message-ID: <200110050246.OAA03493@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5B983AB5F20BD511A3EE0002A52C3CB6E6D6F0@JDM_EXCHANGE.hilversum.endemo
l.com>, Melle.koning@endemol.nl writes:
>Now to use dyndns.org, it is possible to install a client (several are
>availble at dyndns.org), but it seems I could also use xitami for this,
>right?

IIRC Xitami 2.5 (the beta version) includes support for registering with
dynamic DNS servers; it needs a ddnsdef.xml XML file which describes how
to register with the dynamic DNS service.  I suspect this may have been
omitted from the binary packages, but there should be a copy of it in
the source packages available from xitami.com.

>What can be the problem and how can I solve this? The problem is that every
>change I make in the html-admin pages, are not 'saved'. 

The dynamic DNS settings?  Possibly there is a problem with saving
those.  Or are all the settings not saved?

>Is the configuration stored in xml files? I thought it was stored in
>xitami.cfg?

No, the settings are stored in xitami.cfg, defaults.cfg, etc as well as
the aut files.  But some extra information is stored in XML files (like
the dynamic DNS registration information) because they're very flexible,
and there's already code to parse them in Xitami.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 03:50:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 14:50:39 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Bug: SSI Includes aren't recursive
In-Reply-To: Message from Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
 of "Thu, 20 Sep 2001 11:22:39 +0200." <3BA9B55F.7000108@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <200110050250.OAA03575@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3BA9B55F.7000108@freesbee.fr>, Francis Turner writes:
>I just noticed that the SSI include tag (e.g. the one on the testssi 
>page <!--#include file="testssi.inc"-->) cuases the rest of the 
>including document (e.g. testssi.ssi) after the tag not to get delivered 
>if the included document itself uses SSI as the example include does.

The problem is actually with any recursive use of SSI -- there's an
"off-by-one" issue which means that Xitami was storing an
end-of-document marker before the next bit of included SSI, and hence
running into problems.

This is fixed in our version in CVS
(see http://cvs.imatix.com/cgi-bin/viewcvs/)
but not in any of the binaries that have been built.

>Also in the process of debugging and playing I noticed that Xitami has a 
>limit on files with SSI includes of about 35,000+ bytes (one file 
>displayed upto the 35922nd byte, another upto the 35553rd) and any data 
>thereafter is abruptly truncated. 

I think this has also been reported, and I think it may have been fixed
in the version in CVS.

Thanks for the reports.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 03:53:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 14:53:56 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] File upload with xitami???
In-Reply-To: Message from Marc Doigny <marc@verfaillie.com>
 of "Sat, 22 Sep 2001 10:51:53 +0200." <5.0.2.1.2.20010922105137.00a820a0@190.190.190.1>
Message-ID: <200110050253.OAA03644@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.0.2.1.2.20010922105137.00a820a0@190.190.190.1>, Marc Doigny writes:
>The scripts executes correctly (env.exe only prints the windows 
>environment) but where can i find the uploaded file???

If you're uploading via a HTML form, then the uploaded file is part of
the POSTed data that the CGI receives (from the std input file); you'll 
need to parse the file out of that.  There are libraries around for most
languages now which will do much of this automatically for you.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 03:58:17 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 14:58:17 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Regular crash
In-Reply-To: Message from John Poltorak <jp@eyup.org>
 of "Sat, 22 Sep 2001 11:40:29 +0100." <20010922114028.M77@eyup.org>
Message-ID: <200110050258.OAA03704@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20010922114028.M77@eyup.org>, John Poltorak writes:
>#4  0x58753 in _closedir ()
>#5  0x1a99d in close_dir ()

Ah.  I think I know what's going on -- there was a bug in Xitami where
if it failed to open a directory it would still try to call close_dir(),
which would then get very upset because it didn't have a valid directory
handle.

I think this problem is fixed in the version in CVS, as I seem to recall
a bug like this was reported a while ago.

If you want to fix it yourself and rebuild the binary have a look in
smtftpl.c (for ftpc_make_listing()), and change the logic for
opening/closing the directory around so that it only tries to close it
if the open was successful.

>Incidentally, an OS/2 port of GCC v3.0 has just been released and is 
>available here:-
>ftp://unixos2.org/incoming/gcc-os2-3.0-gcc.zip

Interesting.

>I'd be interested in which tools you use for building Xitami on OS/2 as
>I'm hoping to put together an updated set as part of the UnixOS/2 project.

Xitami for OS/2 was built using the EMX compiler suite, plus REXX.  Otto
will generate REXX build scripts (but pre-built versions of these should
already be in the source kits), and Libero is used for generating some
of the other code (again, pre-built versions are in the source kits).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 04:00:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 15:00:05 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] PHP_SELF
In-Reply-To: Message from "roberto" <roberto.bonino@adance.com>
 of "Sun, 23 Sep 2001 19:29:14 +0100." <00b101c1445d$a9238850$0400a8c0@srv1>
Message-ID: <200110050300.PAA03761@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <00b101c1445d$a9238850$0400a8c0@srv1>, "roberto" writes:
>When using the variable PHP_SELF  with xitami , the directory path is
>added again after the file name

I think this is due to the disagreement between Xitami and PHP about how
the URL should be split up into extra path information and filenames,
etc.  ISTR last time it was discussed it was decided that Xitami was
wrong, but there hasn't been a proper release since then, so it's not
fixed.

The XiFusion addon (see http://www.xitami.com/addons.htm) apparently
includes a work around for this.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

this is an Xitami/Pro specific issue, or generic to the Xitami 2.4

directory and try running it like that (after stopping Xitami/Pro).  But

executable over.

From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org

Subject: Re: [Xitami] PHP_SELF 


In message <00b101c1445d$a9238850$0400a8c0@srv1>, "roberto" writes:
>When using the variable PHP_SELF  with xitami , the directory path is
>added again after the file name

I think this is due to the disagreement between Xitami and PHP about how
the URL should be split up into extra path information and filenames,
etc.  ISTR last time it was discussed it was decided that Xitami was
wrong, but there hasn't been a proper release since then, so it's not
fixed.

The XiFusion addon (see http://www.xitami.com/addons.htm) apparently
includes a work around for this.

Ewen

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 15:52:21 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami - Script/File Permissions???
In-Reply-To: Message from "Mike Scholman" <mscholman@hotmail.com>
 of "Tue, 02 Oct 2001 23:23:36 GMT." <F166jvM9KfYDovvQ0Pu00004180@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <200110050352.PAA04633@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

NOTE: Please don't post in HTML to this list; it's very difficult to
deal with when one is replying to the messages.

In message <F166jvM9KfYDovvQ0Pu00004180@hotmail.com>, "Mike Scholman" writes:
>I have set up a Xitami Server on an NT Server with NTFS. I am able to
>run simple PERL and PHP scripts, but if they try to write to disk
>(ie update files, etc...) they fail. 

In which case whichever user it is they are running as does not have
write permissions for the relevant directories.  The relevant user
depends on which version of Xitami you are using (NT service, windows
gui, etc); if you are using the windows GUI version it is the user that
started Xitami running.  If you're using the NT service it's specified
in the service panel (IIRC), and is often the SYSTEM user.

You can assign permissions in NT Server through the GUI as well as with
a command line utility I believe.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Was that an example URL that is different from what is in the HTML?  Or
does it really say "site.com"?  In which case is your domain name
"site.com"?

Also if you're using IE, make sure you turn off the "friendly" error
messages, so that you can see what the webserver is really saying.
Debugging problems with the IE "friendly" error messages is much much
harder.  (Instead of getting a message telling you what went wrong, you
get a message saying basically "nope, that didn't work, guess again".)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 04:47:45 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 15:47:45 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] ftp - chmod
In-Reply-To: Message from Ketil Thorgersen <ketil_thorgersenyahoo.com@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
 of "Wed, 03 Oct 2001 00:48:29 +0200." <5.1.0.14.0.20011003004656.02673c60@pop.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200110050347.PAA04566@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.1.0.14.0.20011003004656.02673c60@pop.mail.yahoo.com>, Ketil Thorgersen writes:
>Is not chmod implemented in the xitami ftp server? When I try, I get a "502 
>- site not implemented" error. Whatever that means?

No, chmod isn't implemented.  IIRC it's done with a special "site"
command (for site specific extensions I think), and Xitami doesn't
implement any of those.  

Basically if you need a more fully featured FTP server you're probably
better using another one that comes with Linux, rather than the fairly
simple one in Xitami.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

 of "Sun, 30 Sep 2001 11:21:21 -0400." <66137859576.20010930112121@iglobal.com>

In message <66137859576.20010930112121@iglobal.com>, xitami writes:
>As a very happy, long time user of Xitami, I accidentally upgraded/installed be
>ta 2.5b1 on our win2000 box (latest SP and patches).  

I'd suggest at least using 2.5b5 (the current beta release) if you do
want to use the beta version.  2.4d9 (the current release version) is
more stable.

>2. Can I load a production version *over* the beta without introducing
>disaster?

You're probably best installing the production version in another
directory and then copying over the configuration files, webpages, etc,
to keep things clean.  In theory it might work to install 2.4d9 over the
top of 2.5b5 but you'll end up with a bunch of extra config files that
don't get used, and it'll be a little confusing.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 04:25:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 15:25:16 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] redirection with header :location
In-Reply-To: Message from Franck Lefebure <mailing@simaho.com>
 of "Wed, 26 Sep 2001 19:16:50 +0200." <5.0.2.1.0.20010926190923.02478470@pop3.simaho.com>
Message-ID: <200110050325.PAA04156@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5.0.2.1.0.20010926190923.02478470@pop3.simaho.com>, Franck Lefebure 
writes:
><?php header ("Location: test.htm")  ?>           doesn't work

This is a server-side redirect.  In theory it might work if the document
is in the root directory; otherwise it won't work with Xitami.  Try
/test.htm, or picking the document path of the existing document and
putting that before the file name you want.

><?php header ("Location: http://127.0.0.1/test.htm")  ?>           is ok

This is a client-side redirect and will "always" work, because the web
browser makes a new request.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 04:23:44 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 15:23:44 +1200
Subject: Re[2]: [Xitami] Xitami too harddisk intensive..
In-Reply-To: Message from Melle Koning <m.koning10@chello.nl>
 of "Tue, 25 Sep 2001 22:17:57 +0200." <4615260297.20010925221757@chello.nl>
Message-ID: <200110050323.PAA04122@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <4615260297.20010925221757@chello.nl>, Melle Koning writes:
>Well yes, I know it is tight. But I chose xitami because I thought it
>had a pretty low memory-footprint(?).

It does have a fairly low memory footprint; about 2MB (at least under
Linux) when it is running. Possible more like 3MB or so under Windows.

>Current situation:
>With "system monitor" w98 reports about 84Megs allocated, but this is
>constantly changing/swapping to 87Mmegs and back to 83Megs.

You're _way_ over committed on your memory for only 28MB of real memory.  
I'm not surprised you're getting fairly poor performance.

>Why on earth would xitami (the only programming 'running') be
>allocating memory and freeing memory so often?

Xitami does have various "background" "threads" which handle various
things which do allocate memory while they're working.  They should be
doing it constantly, but given that you're so massively overcommitted on
your memory, it doesn't surprise me that the whole thing is thrashing.

Seriously: memory is pretty cheap these days.  Even if you need 72pin
SIMMs, they're no where near as expensive as they once were (albeit much
more expensive than generic SDRAM is).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>wake up in the morning, click ok on the 'Xitami Suspended' box, it

I've noticed that one of my copies of Xitami 2.5 seems to get somewhat
upset by various worms poking around.  I've not had a chance to track it
down, but there may be a bug that is being tickled causing it to crash.
(Since the worms are targeting IIS it shouldn't be getting into your

>Xitami, then reinstall it ?

I'd suggest installing the version you want in another directory, and then
copying all your configuration, web pages, etc, etc, over to the new
directory.  When you're happy everything is working in the new
directory, you can just delete the old directory.  (If you're using the
NT Service version you should deregister the service before you delete
the directory to avoid some errors being reported on bootup.)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 05:01:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 16:01:12 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] HTML of WBA Admin Page??
In-Reply-To: Message from "Alvaro E. Siman" <alsiman@cofs.net>
 of "Wed, 03 Oct 2001 20:40:35 -0400." <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCEKKCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <200110050401.QAA04801@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCEKKCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>, "Alvaro E. Siman" wr
ites:
>I want to customize the graphics of the Xitami WBA interface.
>Since I can not find the HTML files responsible for all the pages (Admin,
>Configuration, VHost, ect.) then I am assuming they are dynamically
>generated.

They are dynamically generated in part; most of the text for the
webpages is in the xiadm??.h files.  This is generated from the
xiadmin.fdl file, into a bunch of fml files, which are then generated
into the .h files.

The necessary tools for doing this are available from the Xitami.com
website (http://www.xitami.com/addons.htm) in the SDK.  The rest of the
source is in the source kits also available from the Xitami.com website.

>Is Xitami using a Style Sheet to define color schemes??

No.  It's a really good idea, but the HTML for the admin screens
predates the adoption of a common style sheet language, so it hasn't
been updated to use them.

Updates (to the FDL file) to use a style sheet would be appreciated.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct  5 05:02:19 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 05 Oct 2001 16:02:19 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Aliases, filters and php
In-Reply-To: Message from "Daniel Ajoy" <dajoy@operamail.com>
 of "Wed, 03 Oct 2001 22:27:20 EST." <3BBB90C8.19780.2A88D0@localhost>
Message-ID: <200110050402.QAA04849@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3BBB90C8.19780.2A88D0@localhost>, "Daniel Ajoy" writes:
>I'm having problems when I try to combine and alias with
>a filter to a php file extension.

They don't mix properly at all.  This is a known bug with Xitami.   At
present it's probably best to avoid mixing aliases and filters, and use
something like virtual hosts instead of the aliases (or just copy the
files into a suitable directory which doesn't require an alias).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 10 11:00:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Zdenko =?iso-8859-1?Q?Roh=E1=E8?=)
Date: Wed, 10 Oct 2001 12:00:09 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] WAP-pages
In-Reply-To: <3BC3FFF2.26A6C0A6@sovik.no>
Message-ID: <5.1.0.14.0.20011010115352.00bdaf08@ccsun.tuke.sk>

Hello.
I have found out that you need append lines into defaults.cfg or
to another apropriate config file (into Mime section):

[Mime]
     Wbmp=image/vnd.wap.wbmp
     Wml=text/vnd.wap.wml
     Wmlc=application/vnd.wap.wmlc
     Wmls=text/vnd.wap.wmlscript
     Wmlsc=application/vnd.wap.wmlscriptc

Worked fine for me.
                                 Bye
                                         Zdenko Rohac.

There is one (possible) bug in Xitami, as you have to define Mime-settings in
your virtual host's configuration file. It is not enough to define it just in
the default configuration file.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 10 13:31:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Andrew Morris)
Date: Wed, 10 Oct 2001 13:31:49 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Perl scripts in Windows
In-Reply-To: <3BC43716.A1BFB871@knoop.nl>
Message-ID: <MABBLCOJIONKIIPKCGKLAEGACAAA.andrew.of.morris@talk21.com>

Well, I found Opera and Netscape were fine! For me IE is the really slow
one.
As for your Windows NT error, I'm not sure what this is but it sounds most
likely that it is trying to find Perl.exe and not succeeding. Have you
checked that the location of Perl.exe has been appended to the PATH
environment variable? To find out, simply go to the DOS prompt and type
PATH. In the list of paths you should see the location of perl.exe. If not,
this is probably your problem - although I'm not 100%.
I don't use NT currently, but I did before and it was OK.
Andy

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 10 15:50:24 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 10 Oct 2001 16:50:24 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Perl scripts in Windows
References: <MABBLCOJIONKIIPKCGKLIEFOCAAA.andrew.of.morris@talk21.com>
Message-ID: <3BC46030.3060807@freesbee.fr>


Andrew Morris wrote:

> Has anybody found that Perl scripts run intolerably slow on Windows 98/NT
> with Xitami? I'm using ActivePerl 623 and the problem doesn't appear to be
> specific to the machine or the installation. Even a small test Perl script
> (e.g 'hello world') type stuff takes up to _30 seconds_ to appear in the
> browser. I'm only running this on a local-loop. Does the problem go away
> when you're calling the server from a remote computer?
> Any info or insights appreciated.
> Andy

Using Win 95 and win 98 I have had no problems with perl - I am 
currently using ActiveState v 629 and Xitami 2.5b5 but I have had the 
same results with earlier builds of both.

What I have found is that sometimes when I really run out of memory (I 
have a 64MB machine) then things are very slow. But this is not related 
to perl or Xitami per se.

One other thing that may be is that your perl script is not completing 
correctly and is hanging around. In that case Xitami eventually kills it 
but it takes some time. Finally the 2.5b1 and 2.5b2 versions did not 
pass input to STDIN correctly for CGI scripts. This was fixed in 2.5b4 
and b5 ...

Francis

One more tip for slowness...

sometime windoze takes a long time to resolve the name localhost to the 
loopback IP address. You can verify this and/or fix it by doing a manual 
"ping localhost" in a DOS/CMD prompt before trying the webpage...

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 10 18:33:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 10 Oct 2001 19:33:12 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami Servers
References: <140C571B.442EC269.A20DDBF9@cs.com>
Message-ID: <3BC48658.8090504@freesbee.fr>

If you want Xitami to use the QUERY_STRING environment variable (as 
opposed to passing parameters in STDIN) then you should enable the 
relevant parameter

In the Web based admin this is the "Pass QUERY_STRING?" checkbox in the 
CGI properties page or in the defaults.cfg file have a line of 
form-query=1 in the [CGI] section

You may also wish to provide the URL arguments - in defaults.cfg this is 
enabled with a passargs=1 line.

Francis
PS RTFM -http://localhost/xitami/index4.htm  in the CGI section for 
other relevant info
PPS in 2.5b1 and 2.5b2 the ONLY way to get arguments to the CGI program 
was via QUERY_STRING. If you use perl's CGI.PM then you have to manually 
enable examination of the qeury string (its only semi documented in 
CGI.PM how to do this)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 11 01:43:51 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Wed, 10 Oct 2001 19:43:51 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami Crashing
References: <200110102209.AAA19750@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <3BC4EB47.125CA0FB@2cah.com>

I know you have tried this once before, but..

Make a backup of just your configuration files. Shut Xitami down, delete the
contents of the directory you installed Xitami into. Restart your machine. In
your system32 directory (usually c:\winnt\system32) delete xiwinntc.cpl and
you'll have killed all the remnants of your previous install.

Install Xitami (2.4d9 NT service version) and copy your configuration files
back into the directory you just installed Xitami into.

I'm running the NT service version of 2.4d9 on both a Windows 2000
Professional machine and a Windows 2000 Server machine here without a hitch,
so I know it works.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 11 09:52:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Boyan Brezinsky)
Date: Thu, 11 Oct 2001 10:52:15 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] RE:Perl scripts in Windows (Andrew Morris)
Message-ID: <01C15242.CADEC200.boyan@sanbolic.com>

When I was playing with Bugzilla 2.12, I found the same slowness of perl. I 
couldn't figure out why, I only found the symptoms. Bugzilla is a 
bug-tracking system written in Perl. In version 2.12, there was a script 
that was finding the differences between bug reports - using diff. The 
operation flow was xitami->perl.script1->perl.script2->diff
IIRC, every time xitami called perl, cmd.exe was invoked. In this manner of 
operation the call to diff took 30 seconds to complete, although the 
program itself was ready almost instantly. When I would execute the same 
script (script1) directly from the command line, it completed in the usual 
fast way.
I couldn't resolve this, but thankfully it was done by others - in the 
following versions of Bugzilla diff was dropped, so now it runs just fine 
in the rare occasions that somebody uses it.
System:
Xitami 2.4d9, NT service
Perl ActiveState 5.6.1 - 628
Windows 2000 SP2
128 MB RAM
MySQL 3.23.39 or something like that
diff - from the Cygnus library - ver. 2.7
IE 5.0

So I'd suggest examining which is the component that causes the slowdown. I 
think that 30 seconds was the default timeout of Xitami for processes that 
it perceives as hung. As to why it wouldn't detect the completion of diff, 
or whatever the reason was (I never found it out, as I said) - I don't have 
the slightest idea.
What I did was to turn on the security auditing to find out when each 
process starts and stops, and to turn on the cgi debugging in xitami, so I 
can see when the files were generated.
Maybe in your case it is something to do with paths and exit codes? E.g. if 
a process is called in such a way that it needs to be found via the PATH 
environment variable, its exit code is not correctly passed back? This is 
as wild a guess as it can get, but with all this software you never know.
Best regards,
Boyan

Andrew Morris wrote:

> Has anybody found that Perl scripts run intolerably slow on Windows 98/NT

REGUARDING THE FOLLOWING POST:

>I want to customize the graphics of the Xitami WBA interface.
>Since I can not find the HTML files responsible for all the pages (Admin,
>Configuration, VHost, ect.) then I am assuming they are dynamically

Tey are dynamically generated in part; most of the text for the
.ebpages is in the xiadm??.h files.  This is generated from the
xiadmin.fdl file, into a bunch of fml files, which are then generated
into the .h files.

The necessary tools for doing this are available from the Xitami.com
website (http://www.xitami.com/addons.htm) in the SDK.  The rest of the
source is in the source kits also available from the Xitami.com website.

SIMPLE.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct 12 04:44:53 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 12 Oct 2001 16:44:53 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] HTML of WBA Admin Page??
In-Reply-To: Message from "Alvaro E. Siman" <alsiman@cofs.net>
 of "Thu, 11 Oct 2001 23:33:23 EDT." <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCKELPCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <200110120344.QAA16535@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCKELPCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>, "Alvaro E. Siman" wr
ites:
>>I want to customize the graphics of the Xitami WBA interface. [...]
>They are dynamically generated in part; most of the text for the
>webpages is in the xiadm??.h files.  This is generated from the
>xiadmin.fdl file, into a bunch of fml files, which are then generated
>into the .h files.  [....]
>
>I HAVE DOWNLOADED AND SKIMMED THROUGH THE XIADMIN.FDL FILE.  IT LOOKS PRETTY
>SIMPLE.

Looks like your CAPS lock key got stuck there :-)

>SO IF I DO MAKE CHANGES TO THIS FILE WITH A TEXT EDITOR....WHAT NEXT???
>HOW DO I GET THE CHANGES TO APPLY TO MY CURRENT INSTALLATION???

The basic idea is:
- make changes to the FDL file with a text editor
- run fdlgen xiadmin.fdl
- run fmlgen over each xiadm??.fml file that is generated
- rebuild Xitami from source (including your newly generated files)

You'll need to tools from the Xitami SDK and also a C compiler.  iMatix
uses Microsoft Visual C++ 6.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct 12 05:02:14 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 12 Oct 2001 17:02:14 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami installed files
In-Reply-To: Message from "Alvaro E. Siman" <alsiman@cofs.net>
 of "Thu, 11 Oct 2001 23:53:34 EDT." <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCEMACDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <200110120402.RAA18718@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCEMACDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>, "Alvaro E. Siman" wr
ites:
>I am looking through the Xitami SDK files.  I cant find any of them in my
>Xitami installation.....not even the .gif image files.
>Where does Xitami store the configuration files when it installs itself???

They're all compiled into the binary.  This is part of the reason it's
as big as it is.  The wsxrc program turns the GIF images into an include
file (xiadmin.h).

>If I wanted to replace a button, where would I go??

You need to change the button (from the SDK source), and then run 
wsxrc @xiadmin.rc, and then recompile Xitami.  If you've added images,
you need to edit xiadmin.rc (a text file, one image listed per line) and
add it to the end of that list.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Oct 15 22:11:03 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 16 Oct 2001 10:11:03 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] SysV init script
In-Reply-To: Message from daniel carter <hedonist@win.co.nz>
 of "Tue, 16 Oct 2001 09:52:36 +1300." <3BCB4C94.22CC001@win.co.nz>
Message-ID: <200110152111.KAA01310@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3BCB4C94.22CC001@win.co.nz>, daniel carter writes:
>Has anyone written one of these for xitami? I'd like to have xitami
>installed as a service on my linux box.

It's pretty straight forward to do -- copy an existing one, and then
(a) change to the base directory of Xitami's config files
(b) start xitami as a server "xitami -d"

To kill it, look for the xitami process (there's only one) in the
process table and kill it off.  (Xitami doesn't (yet) write a PID file
unfortunately.)

>Also, is there a way to have xitami running as a non-root user like
>other servers do?  I'd like to have it running as an unprivildged user
>as a security precaution, but i'm running into the port 80 problem.

You can get Xitami to change user after it has started (avoiding the
port 80 problem), by using the [server] setuid functionality.  Certain
things won't work when that's active (eg, restarting the server) because
it no longer has the privileges required to do things like open port 80.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

200 Command okay
150 Preparing to transfer ASCII file
226 Closing data connection

As you can see above, this returns nothing on Xitami.

On the Sun I get the following output:
ftp> ls /dtf-tests/*/*Job.type
200 PORT command successful.
150 ASCII data connection for /bin/ls (192.168.0.3,2072) (0 bytes).
/dtf-tests/test1/DocuJob.type
/dtf-tests/test2/DocuJob.type
/dtf-tests/test3/DocuJob.type
/dtf-tests/test4/DocuJob.type
...
226 ASCII Transfer complete.

The above list response is what the DT needs in order to recognize jobs on
an FTP server.

I assume this problem has to do with the wildcards in the path, because I
can list the files on Xitami using a complete path. However, I have no
control over the formatting of the DT list command. Is there a way to get
Xitami to handle this kind of list request?


- Jeff Hamblin





From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 16 00:34:18 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jeff Hamblin)
Date: Mon, 15 Oct 2001 16:34:18 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] FTP - LIST (ls) not returning wildcarded sub-dirs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 16 03:10:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 15 Oct 2001 22:10:12 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] FTP - LIST (ls) not returning wildcarded sub-dirs
References: <0eeb01c147c3$8f22c560$020aa8c0@Master> <0eff01c147d7$901d3ae0$020aa8c0@Master> <3BB49F45.2282E740@rci.rutgers.edu> <0fd001c14864$fb6e16b0$020aa8c0@Master> <3BB502BA.BCA5E1F8@rci.rutgers.edu> <006201c155d0$01190520$0300a8c0@aplusnet.com>
Message-ID: <3BCB9704.9F5F1E52@rci.rutgers.edu>

> On the Sun I get the following output:
 ftp> ls /dtf-tests/*/*Job.type
 /dtf-tests/test1/DocuJob.type
 /dtf-tests/test2/DocuJob.type

Interesting. Wild-card directory is not specifically supported in
most FTP docs, but my school's Sun's docs have a clue: 

 SunOS 5.5 
 FTP(1)                    User Commands    

  ls [remote-directory] [local-file]
  Print a listing of the contents of a directory  on  the
  remote  machine.   The  listing  includes  any  system-
  dependent  information  that  the  server  chooses   to
  include;  for  example,  most UNIX systems will produce
  output from the command `ls -l'.  ....

That is, ftp on unix is liable to call `ls' directly and pipe it
to the terminal. unix 'ls' typically supports wild directories. 

That can't happen on NT, which has no `ls'. It could call `DIR',
or `DIR /s', but Xitami's cross-platform code tends to avoid
platform-specific calls whenever possible, in favor of simple
universal techniques. 

Since wild-carded directories is kind of an obscure feature, I
suspect you may have to try various FTP servers until you find
one that supports it. If the hint in Sun's FTP docs is correct,
you may have better luck on a unix platform. Be aware that the
Linux default FTP service WS-FTP is notoriously hackable (been
there, been bitten). 

Or, if you grok `c', edit and recompile Xitami's ftp functions to
your liking. The code is neat and clean, but folder globbing is
not necessarily easy to roll from scratch. 

It should be possible to build a FTP service in Perl, with `ls'
features of your choice. I know I could not do it, though. 

 -PRR

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

Subject: [Xitami] installer

In message <DNEFIPOGFKEIMMJIHKLFKEOCCHAA.tinbb@hkplanet.com>, "alex" writes:
>    Can i install Xitami in my client machine without using the installer
>provided by the iMatrix ?

The installer is just an archive (I forget which format the embedded
file is, but I think it's a fairly common archive format), with a
self-extract executable bit at the front, and a tidy bit of "change this
to this" substitution going on in some of the installed files (eg, it
will set up a basic defaults.aut/defaults.cfg).

If you really don't want to use the installer you could either build
Xitami from source, or figure out how to pull the installer package
apart and manually get at the files.

Since the installer just puts stuff in a directory for you, and
configures a few files in that directory, I'm not quite sure why you'd
want to go to the trouble of avoiding using it if you don't want to
build from source.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 16 07:48:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Tue, 16 Oct 2001 07:48:57 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] FTP - LIST (ls) not returning wildcarded sub-dirs
Message-ID: <45498@dsl.co.uk>

In message <006c01c155d1$f8d810c0$0300a8c0@aplusnet.com>
   "Jeff Hamblin" writes:
> 
> > 
> > The DT is sending a list request as follows:
> > ftp> ls \dtf-tests\*\*Job.type
> 
> I pasted in the wrong stuff, it should be:
> 
> The DT is sending a list request as follows:
> ftp> ls /dtf-tests/*/*Job.type
> 
> All slashes are backslashes.

No; those are all SLASHES.  It is the '\' character that is the
backslash.  Don't worry; yours is a very common error in nomenclature
made by those with overexposure to Windoze.  (I'm not quite certain why
this should be; I suspect that the over-use of the backslash as a path
separator has led to many people misnaming it, thus requiring a further
misnaming when referring to the forward slash.)  Of course, you could
always refer to is as a "solidus", which is the official designation in
the national and international character set standards.

I would guess that your problem stems from the fact that NT doesn't know
how to perform wildcard expansion: this is a [non-]feature of the
operating system, and not something that an application, such as an FTP
daemon, can/should be expected to do.

I expect that your Sun performs this by the simple expedient of passing
the LIST command through to activate the standard 'ls -l' program, and
then piping the results back.  This will apply the level of wildcard
expansion that this program knows of.

Your basic problem is that the original FTP client application is
generating these wild-carded requests: is this something that it's
thought of itself?  Or could you write the requests as a series of
scripted operations (perhaps returning a full directory at the current
level, and then working through its constituent sub-directories)?
[That's the approach that I would use with the RxFTP facility if I needed
to script such an FTP client-side operation.]

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 17 15:31:41 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (MATA Tech)
Date: Wed, 17 Oct 2001 10:31:41 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] xitami ftp server problem
In-Reply-To: <PJEIJLBMPLBLPIOEAFAHEEAICEAA.tel-king@gmx.net>
Message-ID: <3BCD5E0D.25239.492156B@localhost>

This is a topic that comes up over and over again, so I will explain 
why it happens and what our company did to "fix" it.  The best part 
is that I will keep the explanation and solution in layman terms.

Xitami's ftp server works fine, actually very well... as long as you 
are not behind a firewall.  File Transfer Protocol is an older transfer 
protocol that, normally, doesn't work well behind a firewall.

Here, we struggled with this back and forth, finally concluding that 
there was no way we could operate without a firewall.  Our first 
compromise was merely to disable the ftp portion of Xitami.  After 
all, from our perspectives, the first time we tried Xitami was based 
on the curiosity of a full-featured web server with a small footprint.  
We had always seen the ftp server as a bonus.

Since that time, we realized that ftp definitely had it's place, 
especially with remote administration.  Our solution was to install a 
separate ftp server that had the capabilities to handle PASV 
transfers from behind a firewall.  In our case, we didnt have much 
time to investigate all the options, so we went on recommendation 
and have great fondness for ServU FTP Server.  I don't want to write 
anything that sounds biased, so I would appreciate if others who 
have chosen alternative ftp options to express what ftp servers they 
have that also work from behind a firewall.  And, if there are any 
situations where people have managed to get Xitami's FTP server 
to work, I am sure everyone at Imatix would appreciate hearing that 
as well, at least for the sake of adding the information to the FAQ.

Personally, I appreciate the power of Xitami.  I know everyone 
wants to have more integrated features added to Xitami.  But, from 
my perspective, what most of the Xitami audience are running are 
the freely available Xitami server.  Therefore, one cannot expect 
Imatix to invest more time (which equates to money) into 
developing more add-ons. When one looks at break-even rationale, 
since we have a retail application for which we paid, an application 
which advertises ftp, not stipulative ftp, I would have to say that I 
would prefer that Imatix spend my money (therefore their time) 
investing in better development of a currently advertised feature and 
having it work to it's fullest potential.

I am getting a nosebleed.... time to get off the soapbox. ;)

Sincerely,
Brad Smith, President/CFO
Social Design Technologies

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 17 21:00:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 17 Oct 2001 16:00:16 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami and Windows NT - how do I name ???
References: <6FDE0867413DD21182BF00A0C972519207558FF7@MSWG4.bwc.state.oh.us>
Message-ID: <3BCDE350.87B1F02D@rci.rutgers.edu>

> The cart program asks for two main items of information - the "document root" which is simply the path to where it lives - c:\xitami\cgi-bin\cart.cgi - and the "domain name" - which, is where on a unix server at my ISP would be something like www.smart-choices.org (which really does exist, and where the cart programs are located), but I'm not sure what that value needs to be on my local system. 

"domain name" of "localhost" should work. Same as you should be using to
open the web pages that call your scripts. 

If you prefer to see a "normal looking" URL like "snoo.com" in your
scripts, edit your "hosts" file like this: 

 127.0.0.1       localhost
 127.0.0.1       ads.x10.com  #damn spam
 127.0.0.1       snoo.com     # for testing cart program

(Some Windows distributions come with no "hosts", just "hosts.sam". Copy
it to the right name, re-start your browser or maybe Windows.) 

The first line is why "localhost" resolves to "this machine", and is
normally preset in "hosts". (The second line is my trick to foil a
specific pop-up ad server-- ignore it.) The third line say that all
calls to "snoo.com" should go to the local machine. 

If there is a real "snoo.com" (or whatever test-name you use), this will
of course prevent you from reaching them. You could in fact use your
real name "127.0.0.1 www.smart-choices.org" for testing from your local
machine, and comment it out (leading "#") when you want to test from the
real machine. Changes in "hosts" -may- work immediately, or with full
browser re-start. In the past, on WinNT4, I could keep hosts open,
change things, and see results in Netscape instantly. 

One issue: some versions of Windows will insist on connecting to an
external DNS server even to resolve names set locally in the "hosts"
file. If you are on-line, not a problem, but if you work on a laptop at
the beach it can be frustrating when it tries to dial-out just to "find
itself". 

Disclaimer: MicroSoft never understood TCP/IP or DNS well, so your
results may vary depending on Windows version, service pack, browser
version, and moon-phase. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 18 02:36:03 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 18 Oct 2001 14:36:03 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Web port 8080 and FTP
In-Reply-To: Message from Raymond Judge <RayJudge@optonline.net>
 of "Wed, 17 Oct 2001 21:06:49 EDT." <9177F5D4FF30D511BDAC00A0C9B856BF049412@762NATO>
Message-ID: <200110180136.OAA27429@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <9177F5D4FF30D511BDAC00A0C9B856BF049412@762NATO>, Raymond Judge writes:
>I am forced to use port 8080 to run my Xitami web server due to firewall
>restrictions from my cable provider.  I would still like to run my FTP
>service on port 21, yet when I run Xitami enabling the FTP service it
>unavailable on port 21.  Any suggestions?

The only way to run HTTP on port 8080 in Xitami at present, is to set
the "port base" to 8000; which shifts _everything_ up by 8000.  So FTP
becomes 8021.  As a hack you can move FTP back down by giving it a
negative value (== 21-8000 = 7979).

Adding a better way of just moving the HTTP service is on our todo list.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

I think most of the people that are running a small server are not
necessarily using it for commerce.....they just want an easy and simple way
to get their web pages up.  That said, most people who do this on their
spare time would certainly appreciate any remote administration or time
saving features.

2.) I would guess that the majority of people who want your server, dont
necessarily want it just because it is free.  I know that I would love to
see an easy to use, but feature rich server for under $300.oo.  It is still
a lot of money, but it is better than the several thousand dollars of IIS
and other servers.

3.) I would also guess that the majority of the people who want an easy to
install/use server are NOT IT PROFFESSIONALS.  My guess is that many of them
do not know how to program, and just want the easy to use Web Admin screens,
and not the config files for configuration.

4.) After using the free Xitami, I would be willing to pay for more features
for an upgrade.  I just have no need for SSL.  I am just interested in
serving up cool pages, not commerce.  I would love to see features that
allow me to use Macromedia Dreamweaver, Microsoft Front Page, and Adobe Go
Live with Xitami.  Obviously, if you cant set up FTP then you cant use
either Macromedia or Adobe products for administration.....or at least it
becomes very hard to do to the point that their benefits are nullified.
Considering that the option of Front Page has already been taken away, then
eliminating the other two options is a bigt drawback for Xitami.

5.) An application server that is integral to Xitami is indispensible.  I
dont understand the logic of offering SSL for secure shopping carts, but not
the engines/servers that make the shopping cart work.  ASP and JSP servers
are necessary.

Last but not least: Offer your clients to buy only the options they need.
This is why people dont like Microsoft IIS.  It is overcomplicated and full
of stuff that you dont need BUT WERE FORCED TO PAY FOR.  If you can offer a
base package with incremental add-ons (each with a price) I think you would
really please your following.  I am certainly willing to pay for more
features beyond that of the free Xitami.

Alvaro Siman

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of MATA Tech
Sent: Wednesday, October 17, 2001 10:32 AM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: Re: [Xitami] xitami ftp server problem


This is a topic that comes up over and over again, so I will explain
why it happens and what our company did to "fix" it.  The best part
is that I will keep the explanation and solution in layman terms.

Xitami's ftp server works fine, actually very well... as long as you
are not behind a firewall.  File Transfer Protocol is an older transfer
protocol that, normally, doesn't work well behind a firewall.

Here, we struggled with this back and forth, finally concluding that
there was no way we could operate without a firewall.  Our first
compromise was merely to disable the ftp portion of Xitami.  After
all, from our perspectives, the first time we tried Xitami was based
on the curiosity of a full-featured web server with a small footprint.
We had always seen the ftp server as a bonus.

Since that time, we realized that ftp definitely had it's place,
especially with remote administration.  Our solution was to install a
separate ftp server that had the capabilities to handle PASV
transfers from behind a firewall.  In our case, we didnt have much
time to investigate all the options, so we went on recommendation
and have great fondness for ServU FTP Server.  I don't want to write
anything that sounds biased, so I would appreciate if others who
have chosen alternative ftp options to express what ftp servers they
have that also work from behind a firewall.  And, if there are any
situations where people have managed to get Xitami's FTP server
to work, I am sure everyone at Imatix would appreciate hearing that
as well, at least for the sake of adding the information to the FAQ.

Personally, I appreciate the power of Xitami.  I know everyone
wants to have more integrated features added to Xitami.  But, from
my perspective, what most of the Xitami audience are running are
the freely available Xitami server.  Therefore, one cannot expect
Imatix to invest more time (which equates to money) into
developing more add-ons. When one looks at break-even rationale,
since we have a retail application for which we paid, an application
which advertises ftp, not stipulative ftp, I would have to say that I
would prefer that Imatix spend my money (therefore their time)
investing in better development of a currently advertised feature and
having it work to it's fullest potential.

I am getting a nosebleed.... time to get off the soapbox. ;)

Sincerely,
Brad Smith, President/CFO
Social Design Technologies

Subject: [Xitami] Question - 502 error message
Message-ID: <6FDE0867413DD21182BF00A0C97251920755900A@MSWG4.bwc.state.oh.us>

I've got xitami installed on a windows NT 4.0 system with plenty of hard

as well. Browser is IE 6 with the option to not use the proxy server for
addresses beginning with xxx.moo.com taken. xxx.moo.com is defined in my
hosts file as 127.0.0.1 as well as localhost having that address. Other

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 18 21:34:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Thu, 18 Oct 2001 21:34:15 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Standalone and DOS
Message-ID: <45517@dsl.co.uk>

In message <005901c157b8$7e59ae10$b82e9c3e@ednic>
   joubin.far@t-online.de (Joubin Far) writes:

> I have copied " hosts file " into winnt\system32\drivers\etc\hosts folder
> for my virtual hosts.
> Now if i want to access to an address eg. www.jf.com ( a virtual host
> address and it was implemented into hosts file)
> it dosent happen in standalone mod but by dialing via my ISP.
> Standalone only works for localhost.
> Can someone tell me the reason?

Yes: as was remarked only yesterday, MICROS~1 haven't the foggiest idea
about TCP/IP, and especially not about the niceties of the hosts file vs.
DNS.  Consequently, their so-called operating systems (even the fancy
shiny new ones like XP) do the wrong thing; even when you do your utmost
to assist them in doing "the right thing", they second-guess you and
assume that "you know nothing: THIS is the way it's done".

Using OS/2, I could handle your situation by setting the environment
variable USEHOSTSFIRST; however, because I have to suffer the
co-existence of various Windoze boxen on my home LAN, I now run a full
caching nameserver on my OS/2 server, which can satisfy this sort of
request from the Windoze machines.  When it really DOES need details of a
domain that is not in its local database or cache, then, and only then,
does it call my ISP's nameservers (because the boot.db file contains the
relevant forwarders line).

Now Win2K comes complete with a pretend implementation of a DNS server
(you're probably better off forcing it NOT to run "from data in the
registry", when the full expertise of "DNS & BIND" can be applied
verbatim) which could probably achieve your goal: however, I think you'd
find better advice on this on a newsgroup or mailing list related to
running DNS under Windows.

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk

    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 18 23:13:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 18 Oct 2001 18:13:12 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] xitami ftp server problem
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCGEMPCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <3BCF53F8.F6C77BC4@rci.rutgers.edu>

Alvaro - 

> As a customer I think you would appreciate hearing ....

I'm an unpaying user, not The Company, but I'll jump in and say things
Ewen may not want to say.

[I see Brad got in first with comments similar to mine, but maybe I have
something to add.]

First, it is clear that development of Xitami is stalled. Imatix
primarily does custom software. Xitami grew out of an early project, and
was released to promote Imatix's ability. Since then, Imatix apparently
has got so much good paying custom work that Ewen is chained to his desk
for days at a time, too busy to even peek at this mail-list or take time
to release Xitami updates (or even get all their websites to point to
the latest releases). I gather that they also moved or renovated their
headquarters, another sign that the custom software business is being
very good to Imatix. I'm happy for them; but that means Xitami is what
it is and won't get much attention. 

I believe that Xitami was released with the hopes that a strong user
community would develop improvements. Such has been the case with Apache
and Linux; but not with Xitami. It seems to draw simpletons like me: I
can write 3-line BASIC programs, and I have changed a string in the
Xitami code and got it to compile, but when I try to change how it works
the compiler laughs at me. There are some far better programmers using
Xitami, and some improvements come from them, but most of them are busy
on their own projects. 

>  I would guess that the majority of people who want your server, dont
necessarily want it just because it is free.  

I disagree. I think most Xitami users like "free". Even at that bargain
price there is strong competition from free Apache. 

> want the easy to use Web Admin screens, and not the config files for configuration.

That, for me, was the key distinction between Xitami and Apache.
Apache's config files are huge, full of things that I don't understand,
and the key items are not grouped together. However, considering the
versatile and advanced state of Apache over Xitami, it would make more
sense for someone to sit down and write a Web-GUI interface for Apache's
config files than to try to add all possible features into Xitami. 

> several thousand dollars of IIS and other servers.

MS sent me IIS for free; I have no idea why. It also comes "free" with
the high price versions of NT. Or if you do not need something quite
that heavy, MS PWS (a cut-down IIS) has always been a free download and
works OK. But at -any- price, my opinion of PWS/IIS is that it was
written by children to $ell other software (Front Page, Access, Back
Office, etc etc). 3 years ago I suspected it was buggy hacker-bait, and
CodeRed shows my suspicions were right. It also locks you into MS O/Ses
and backend applications and Intel-ish hardware, whereas many other
servers are multi-platform. At any price, IIS is too expensive. 

> A better FTP is definetly one of them, as opposed to SSL capabilities.

I find the FTP to be quite adequate. Not 100%: it sometimes chokes on
large/many files, someone here says it lacks wildcard directory listing,
and its portbase is locked to the HTTP portbase. Still, except for
weekend crashes when one of my associates tries to upload a month's
worth of vacation pictures in one sitting, I'm happy with it. 

Note that the world is FULL of FTP servers, many of them very
feature-rich, many free. It is no problem to disable Xitami's FTP,
install another FTP service, and point it to the same folder as your
webpages. 

Since the world offers many good free and inexpensive FTP servers, and
many of us make zero income from our servers, charging for a spiffy FTP
feature in Xitami does not seem like a good business plan. However, a
need for SSL almost proves that you are making money with your web
server, so it is quite reasonable to charge for the SSL module. 

> features that allow me to use .... Microsoft Front Page, 

??? A colleague is learning FP, I told her to point to my Xitami server,
and -bam- her pages published. On Xitami, FP "Extensions" are not
supported, but these are buggy MS DLLs that I don't want laying around
in public. I admit I have not much explored what FP can do when dancing
with IIS..... it may do some fun stuff but I also smell hacker-doors. 

>  ASP and JSP servers are necessary.

MS's implementation of ASP is proprietary and was uncommon when Xitami
was developed. The same things can be done with SSI, PHP, and other
techniques that don't require you to sleep with Bill Gates. If you
already have MS ASP pages and "can't afford to change", then you have
already fallen into Bill Gates' trap. You Can Be Saved; but you have to
want to. A choice each of us must make alone. 

> offer a base package with incremental add-ons

Imatix seems to be a bunch of programmers, not order-clerks. Their core
business model is "We'll do this whole business system for $10,000". 3
months of programmer work, 3 hours to type a bill and deposit the check.
I don't think they want to handle a lot of small customers and spend
most of their time supporting dumb questions; that's not the best use of
good programmers like Imatix has. 

Also, even if you only buy 3 of 10 modules, those modules have to be
tested in all combinations so that no matter what collection you get,
they will work together. Testing many configurations adds costs. I think
"dinner with or without dessert" is a better menu than mix-and-match
ala-carte. Obviously this could go either way, but I don't think Imatix
wants to run a cafeteria. 

My 2 cents, and only my opinion.

 -PRR

Yech. Windows File Sharing is horrible. Plus the question was about Xitami, 
and using \\server\share completely ignores Xitami :-)

> 	Can i not use http://www.website.classroom for example.

Get your server's IP address (192.168.0.1 or whatever - run winipcfg or ipconfig, depending on your Windows version).

On the client PCs, type in the URL http://<server IP address>/whatever/, for example http://192.168.0.1/ for the index page or http://192.168.0.1/xitami for the Xitami online docs or whatever.


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct 19 16:43:23 2001

> upload a file via HTTP-PUT. .. Xitami won't let me upload files larger than a couple of KBytes (around 10KB).  my host's Apache-server works 
fine....

Guessing in the dark: Is your machine Windows? (What version?) Is the
host on unix? NT?

A limit like 10K sounds like your script is passing the body of the file
through the command line and "environment". That could be less than 1K
in DOS, somewhat bigger in Win9x, very large in WinNT, and large and
often essentially unlimited in unix. 

I'm not familiar enough with HTTP-PUT or PHP to know how to check or
modify that... I'm just hoping this jogs the memory of someone who is
more expert in such things.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct 19 17:14:03 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Yancy Shepherd)
Date: Fri, 19 Oct 2001 11:14:03 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Problem with cgi-bin
Message-ID: <B7F5BB7A.5C5%yancy@print-imaging.com>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Oct 19 20:48:43 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 19 Oct 2001 15:48:43 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Problem with cgi-bin
References: <B7F5BB7A.5C5%yancy@print-imaging.com>
Message-ID: <3BD0839B.2CF9499C@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  didn't install a cgi-bin. Is that supposed to happen?

Yes. 

That threw me too.

The customary default CGI programs are now considered potential security
risks. "testcgi" has hints of your O/S, paths, script local path, temp
folder, and other clues that "might" aid a hacker. While an environment
report has always been a standard web server tool, current advice from
most security experts is you should not have stuff like that exposed
except for testing. 

Since that's about all that came in Xitami's cgi-bin distribution
folder, for 2.49 they choose to just omit the whole folder. 

Obviously you can create a cgi-bin for your own scripts. (You could even
be clever and use a different name, so hackers who know Xitami won't
quickly find it.)

If you need the old testcgi script, someone here can probably send it to
you or you can extract an older release of Xitami into a scrap
directory. 

 -PRR

Subject: [Xitami] Windows XP?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Ken Joy" <kenjoy@kenjoy.com>

In message <NEBBLFLLGLJLCLICPHLDAEELCIAA.kenjoy@kenjoy.com>, "Ken Joy" writes:
>Hi, I'm new to the list, and sorry if this has been asked and answered, but
>will Xitami run under Windows XP?  I'm thinking about upgrading to XP soon.

As far as we know Xitami should run just as well on Windows XP as it
does on earlier versions.  The NT Service version should even work there
if you prefer that version.

Ewen

Paul Reid wrote:

>>upload a file via HTTP-PUT. .. Xitami won't let me upload files larger than a couple of KBytes (around 10KB).  my host's Apache-server works 
>>
>fine....
>
>Guessing in the dark: Is your machine Windows? (What version?) Is the
>host on unix? NT?
>
>A limit like 10K sounds like your script is passing the body of the file
>through the command line and "environment". That could be less than 1K
>in DOS, somewhat bigger in Win9x, very large in WinNT, and large and
>often essentially unlimited in unix. 
>
>I'm not familiar enough with HTTP-PUT or PHP to know how to check or
>modify that... I'm just hoping this jogs the memory of someone who is
>more expert in such things. 
>
> -PRR
>
Sorry, my fault not to mention the OS.
I'm running WinME (de) and Xitami 2.4d6
The host on the other side is propably a Linux-system running Apache.
The PHP version is 4.0.6 on both sides.

As far as I can see the file is not passed through the environment, as a temporary file is created. For debuggin purposes I output the name and path of the temp file and it seems to be complete.

Any more ideas?

Thx

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Oct 21 20:55:22 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (RUNE FARESTVEIT)
Date: Sun, 21 Oct 2001 21:55:22 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] UltraDev , asp and Xitami
References: <000e01c15a63$5a1e93a0$378b68d5@oemcomputer>
Message-ID: <001301c15a6a$5248a3d0$bcc1d9c1@killer>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0010_01C15A7B.154F99A0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Well to be frank... you have a problem.
Since xitami never did support asp code you will never be able to run an =
asp page on your xitami server.
I uses the Ultradev to develop asp apps myself but had to trade me =
xitami for an PWS :(=20
I have heard roumers about numbers of "asp-addons" event for the xitami =
but have not so far found any that did work.
If you want to stay with the xitami i recomend PHP as the language,if =
not get pws (WARNING that 1 is EXTREAMLY unstable under W98) Better get =
W2k and iis5 if you really want to work with aspcode.

Rune
www.aspdesign.no

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Oct 22 10:16:30 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jim Gardner)
Date: Mon, 22 Oct 2001 02:16:30 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [Xitami] Cannot find CGI script
Message-ID: <20011022091630.46663.qmail@web10008.mail.yahoo.com>

--0-1963152090-1003742190=:45984
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii


Can anyone please help me with a problem I'm having.  I'm new to Xitami and I'm trying to get it to test a simple Perl script (I've only just started to leaen Perl).  I've looked through the Xitami online FAQ with no luck.  I am running v2.4d9 on a Windows Me machine.  I haven't changed any of the settings, I simply downloaded and installed.  I have also installed Perl (to the default directory of C:\Perl ) and have written an extremely simple script (just displays a line of text) which is located in the C:\Xitami\Webpages\cgi-bin directory.  The script starts with the usual "#!C:/Perl/bin/perl" line (which is where the Perl interpreter is located).  I have published my site locally to C:\Xitami\Webpages and I can navigate around the site perfectly by using http://localhost/index.html in my browser (MSIE 5.0).  However when I click a button to run the cgi the browser cannot find it ("The page cannot be found"  Error 400 - Bad request) even though the file is definitely there!  The URL shows the correct address (" http://localhost/cgi-bin/firscript.cgi") and the file is also present when I look in Windows Explorer.  Why does MSIE5.0 not find the script file???

I'm absoulutely stuck - it must be a simple problem but I don't know where to go next.


Regards 

Jim Gardner 

E-Mail (Home) jim@jimgardner.co.uk

InstantASP is NOT Xitami's solution; if you follow the link, you'll
realize that it's written by a different company.  Moreover, there is a
free evaluation version, so try before you buy.

I did try this about 6 months ago, hoping to move away from IIS for a
course we teaching.  Sadly, at that time, InstantASP did not handle some
perfectly common ASP objects, and so was not viable.  They promised a
revision shortly; I haven't looked to see if it's been published as yet.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Oct 22 19:25:23 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Johnson, Nathan J)
Date: Mon, 22 Oct 2001 14:25:23 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Servlets (JSP) in Xitami!
Message-ID: <9EFD49E2FB59D411AABA0008C7E675C005FB6B28@emss04m10.ems.lmco.com>

Mihaela,

It sounds like you are having a CLASSPATH problem.  Make sure that your
servlet class is the classpath.  What I usually do is package my servlets in
a jar file and then use the "java -classpath" option to specify my jar file
when I launch the servletrunner.  I also do not use the .class extension in
my servlet.properties file.  Hopefully this helps.

~Nate Johnson

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Oct 22 19:13:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Mon, 22 Oct 2001 19:13:39 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Servlets (JSP) in Xitami!
Message-ID: <45575@dsl.co.uk>

In message <003901c15b44$b95c1d10$6f01a8c0@irionmihaela>
   "Mihaela Chistruga" writes:
> Thank you very much!
> 
> I already downloaded Servlet Runner and I'm trying now to configure it, b
> ut
> I have a problem: it seems that I don't know how to specify the full name
>  of
> the class that implements the servlet or I don't know where to put the
> class, because I keep getting the message:
> 
> Oct 22, 2001 2:56:49 PM iMatix Servlet Runner -- started
> Oct 22, 2001 2:56:49 PM synonyms: servlet class not found (Synonyms)
> 
> and my properties file looks like this:
> 
> servlet.synonyms.code = Synonyms.class
> 
> Both the properties file and the class file are in the same directory!
> 
> Please give me a hint!

The hint I immediately think of with Java is that the filenames are case
sensitive; whilst Windoze is quite happy with any spelling of source and
class names, java.exe and similar programs all look for the file with the
exact spelling.  It can be very confusing on a computer that, like
Windows (or, for that matter, OS/2 with HPFS) can permit filenames to be
written in upper, lower or mixed case, and yet the filesystem itself will
find the file with any form of the letters.

Could that be a factor here (I know nothing about supporting JSP through
ServletRunner)?

The other idea that springs to mind is do you have a CLASSPATH
environment variable?  If this does not include '.', the current
directory, classes will only be sought in the directories listed in the
path; this is a security feature.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 23 09:51:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Tue, 23 Oct 2001 09:51:39 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Re: [Xitami/off-topic] attn: Alvaro Siman
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Mon, 22 Oct 2001 18:46:57 EDT."
 <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCKENICDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCKENICDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <E15vxHf-0003CK-00@entropy.ucam.org>

He's complaining about your HTML e-mail. HTML mails are around three times 
as big as plain text ones, are rarely any more useful (most of the time 
they just enable people to send you uglier and more intrusive spam), and if 
you look at them in a non-HTML e-mail client, they appear twice: once in 
plain text and once in badly written HTML (since it's automatically written 
by Outlook and isn't efficiently coded at all).

Subject: [Xitami] is Xitami hack-proof?

References: <20011023033358.17902.cpmta@c012.sfo.cp.net>

It's one of the recent IIS viruses trying to escape from the server root, 
run cmd.exe (NT's version of command.com (DOS) or /bin/sh (Unix)), and get 
a directory listing ("cmd.exe /c dir") in preparation for further cracking. 
This is not because your server is infected, it's because someone else's is.


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 23 10:03:41 2001

In message <002b01c15ba0$39311ee0$0c1efea9@main>, "Ashfield Web Services Ltd" wr
ites:
>How do I change the File Permissions (755,666 etc....) for files in the
>cgi-bin. [...] Windows 98 SE

You can't :-)  Windows doesn't support file permissions like that.  Any
program, and any user, can do anything they like under Windows.  So just
ignore the instructions about needing to change file permissions;
they're for Unix/Linux (and to a lesser extent Windows NT which uses a
slightly different model).

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 23 13:50:35 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Tue, 23 Oct 2001 13:50:35 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Netscape 6 (or Mozilla) and /admin
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Tue, 23 Oct 2001 14:16:00 +0200."
 <3BD55F80.9020703@gmx.net>
References: <3BD55F80.9020703@gmx.net>
Message-ID: <E15w10t-0003P1-00@entropy.ucam.org>

I had this problem with Mozilla 0.95 on Linux; since Netscape 6.1 is a 
modified version of an earlier Mozilla build, it makes sense that you get 
the same problem. Disable Javascript in defaults.cfg by editing it with 
Notepad (I think German Windows calls it "Editor") and adding this:

------------------- begin
[Console]
    Javascript = "0"
------------------- end

The WBA should work nicely after that. It works for me, anyway.
