From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 23 17:34:30 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 23 Oct 2001 12:34:30 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami and coldfusion Express
References: <3BD594B9.4165ED7F@borkowetz.com>
Message-ID: <3BD59C16.731E49D0@rci.rutgers.edu>

> on the disk c:\ and everything.. work fine. For a performance test, I have done the same on a Pentium I PC but on disk d:\ (c:\ is full) but noting works...

Most operating systems don't have CP/M-type "disk letters" and multiple
roots; many cross-platform scripts can be baffled by this. 

Sometimes you just need to go through ALL your settings and make sure
they have drive letters. 

> disk c:\ 

Tip: when setting up webservers and their frills, unless told otherwise,
only use the forward-slash "/" to define paths, even on DOS\Windows. In
almost all cases, this works (even at a Windows command line); C and
Perl programmers use "\" for something else so if they didn't handle the
DOS case perfectly the \-ed path gets mangled. 

For your quickie performance test: it may be easiest to move some stuff
off of C: to D:, then install your scripts on C:. When tested, move
stuff back. Mass-copying may be quicker than wondering why the program
does not like "D:\". 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 23 17:35:41 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Tue, 23 Oct 2001 18:35:41 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] chmodd's for cgi - help please
References: <200110230903.WAA17514@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz> <000c01c15bbd$71655f20$0c1efea9@main>
Message-ID: <3BD59C5D.5070701@freesbee.fr>

Ashfield Web Services Ltd wrote:

>Thanks for reply.
>
>That is how I understood it but I have got a situation that when running a
>cgi script I get the error "can't write to fileX.etc ....check permissions"
>
Ummm.

If you are running a perl CGI script and the perl CGI script in question 
is trying to read or modify a file in a non-existent directory then it 
may be returning an error that is then mangled like this.

For example if you do an
  open <FILE> ">/usr/tmp/tmpfile" somewhere in your script but you have 
no /usr/tmp directory - which is rarely the case in windows - then you 
will get an error about the inability to open a file which may then try 
and helpfully suggest you need permissions changed when actually what 
you need to do is either create the directories /usr and /usr/tmp/ or 
(better) change the path to something suitable such as /windows/TEMP/. 
By the way it is worth noting that activestate perl is pretty relaxed 
about / and \ as is Xitami so its better to use / unless you really have 
to speciff C:\windows\temp\filename because zou have to pass this to a 
command shell.

Francis

PS the below perl function is one I use to create paths for files that 
may not have one. remove the print statements if you don't want to be 
warned that this is happening

# utility function to create directory tree if it doesn't exist.
# example usage:  pavePath('/results/http/site/dir/subdir/file.htm')
#   will create as many of
# /results/,
# /results/http/,
# /results/http/site/,
# /results/http/site/dir/
# and /results/http/site/dir/subdir/ as required
# arguably it may be more efficient to start from the full path and work 
backwards?
sub pavePath {
    my ($fQname) = @_;
    return if (-d(substr ($fQname,0,rindex($fQname,'/')))); # if path 
exists quit now
    my ($ch) = index($fQname,'/',1); # avoid trying to create the / 
directory!
    print 'paving...';
    while($ch>=0) {
        mkdir(substr($fQname,0,$ch)) unless -d(substr($fQname,0,$ch));
        print substr ($fQname,0,$ch),":\n";
        $ch=index($fQname,'/',$ch+1);
    }
}

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Oct 23 18:49:13 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Tue, 23 Oct 2001 18:49:13 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami and coldfusion Express
Message-ID: <45583@dsl.co.uk>

In message <3BD59C16.731E49D0@rci.rutgers.edu> Paul Reid writes:

> Tip: when setting up webservers and their frills, unless told otherwise,
> only use the forward-slash "/" to define paths, even on DOS\Windows. In
> almost all cases, this works (even at a Windows command line); C and
> Perl programmers use "\" for something else so if they didn't handle the
> DOS case perfectly the \-ed path gets mangled. 

Errm, paths with forward slashes are accepted just about anywhere in
Windoze *except* in a command window; there, the forward slash introduces
switches (cf. with use of '-' in Unix).  Certainly internally all the
file manipulation functions and APIs do indeed accept forward slashes.
But not in an "MS-DOS Prompt".  Once upon a time, one could run a little
utility program which changed the "switch character", which is held in
one byte within DOS's interrupt vector, and thus use '-' to introduce
switches on a command-line: one could then indeed use '/' as a path
separator.

Sadly, MICROS~1 deliberately broke this at DOS V5.0, so even if the
vector content is changed, command windows still only accept '\' as a
path separator.

However, I fully support your viewpoint that ONLY the forward slash
should be used within configuration files; only use a backslash (which
might require escaping as "\\") in situations where the forward slash is
unacceptable to some bit of Windoze code.

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 24 20:20:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Andrew Morris)
Date: Wed, 24 Oct 2001 12:20:55 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] is Xitami hack-proof?
In-Reply-To: <2D123C9B36C5D31182B90090279CF9A65A6648@CLIFFY>
Message-ID: <NFBBKNEOIPAFKHLMLGMBOEEGCAAA.andrew.of.morris@talk21.com>

I read an article recently about how hackers can get into IIS systems using
Unicode sequences (such as the %255c shown below), which IIS does not
process correctly and causes it to allow access to areas of the hard disk
which should be under security. Looks like a hacker is trying to view your
root directory contents by executing the DIR command using cmd.exe...

 - Excerpt from article -
Top Vulnerabilities to Windows Systems (W)
W1 - Unicode Vulnerability (Web Server Folder Traversal)
W1.1 Description:
Unicode provides a unique number for every character, no matter what the
platform, no matter what the program, no matter what the language. The
Unicode Standard has been adopted by most vendors, including Microsoft. By
sending an IIS server a carefully constructed URL containing an invalid
Unicode UTF-8 sequence an attacker can force the server to literally walk
up and out of a directory and execute arbitrary scripts. This type of
attack is also known as the directory traversal attack.

The Unicode equivalents of / and \ which are %2f and %5c, respectively.
However, you can also represent these characters using so-called "overlong"
sequences. Overlong sequences are technically invalid Unicode
representations that are longer than what is actually required to represent
the character. Both / and \ can be represented with a single byte. An
overlong representation, such as %c0%af for / represents the character using
two bytes. IIS was not written to perform a security check on overlong
sequences. Thus, passing an overlong Unicode sequence in a URL, will bypass
Microsofts security checks. If the request is made from a directory marked
as "executable" the attacker can cause the executable files to be executed
on the server. Additional information on the Unicode threat can be found at:

http://www.wiretrip.net/rfp/p/doc.asp?id=57&face=2


The full URL of the article is at http://66.129.1.101/top20.htm

Hope this helps...I'm not expert but your e-mail reminded me of the article.
Looks like its only an IIS threat anyway.
Andy

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 24 18:28:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Wed, 24 Oct 2001 13:28:16 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] is Xitami hack-proof?
References: <2D123C9B36C5D31182B90090279CF9A65A6648@CLIFFY>
Message-ID: <3BD6FA30.20DF72EA@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  is Xitami hack-proof?

Nothing is hack-proof. 

Let's look at what a hacker can do:

 1) crash your server. Most complex software has some combination of
unexpected input that will confuse it to death. Older versions of Xitami
on DOS/Win would lock-up if you request the file "/LPT1"... it waits
forever for the printer to supply data. But there are ways to make your
server inaccessible no matter what software it runs; ping-floods are a
popular trick.

 2) read your secret data. A good webserver on a good O/S has a very
clear policy about what files may or may not be served. I have not heard
of any Xitami hacks like this, and only one minor Apache hack. IIS seems
to have a big loophole in how it parses invalid meta-characters and a
carefully designed URL can read anything on an unpatched IIS machine. 

 3) infect your server. Install the hacker's code to run on your
machine, either to aid in an attack on another machine or to give the
hacker access to your secret files. It isn't that easy to make a
computer run arbitrary code. The easiest way is to find a telnet login
with no password and ample permissions. Another way is to hit a
protected login with a VERY long username or password that overflows the
login code and inserts malicious code where it will be run; this
requires specific knowledge of the binary code behind the login. CodeRed
exploits something like that in how IIS handles URL query-strings. 

Note that a specific attack on the "wrong" machine may have unintended
side-effects. CodeRed does not infect H-P printers, but a CodeRed attack
can cause the printer to lock-up and need a re-boot. 

However, Xitami is well designed (simple direct code), and is too
uncommon to attract hacker's direct interest. The only side-effect of
CodeRed attacks is bloated log files. I'd rather watch my logs grow than
suffer the pains of IIS operators. 

Most hacks have to target specific flaws in the server-- the hacker has
to know the insides of the code or behavior. For best effect, hackers
study the most-used servers: Apache and IIS. Apache is fairly clean and
has a large support community capable of quick patches. IIS is a mess
and it takes MS a long time to even admit there is a problem. (There are
a few other big servers popular for e-Commerce, like iPlanet, and these
are targeted by hackers to gain money-info.)

We don't know how many vulnerabilities exist in Xitami. But Xitami has
NO code in common with the hacker-favorites, Apache and IIS, so attacks
that work on the big servers are not liable to infect Xitami. Even if a
CodeRed-type worm were possible on Xitami, it would have a fairly hard
time finding another Xitami server to infect. 

 "GET /msadc/..%255c..
 "GET /scripts/..%c1%1c../

Someone is trying to exploit IIS's directories and flaws. They are too
dumb to notice that yours is not a IIS server. (These attacks are
automated; it is quicker to poke blindly than to check to see if the
target is the right brand.)

-OR-... your network administrator is testing to see if any machines on
her subnets are potential targets of a CodeRed-type attack. My
university has been "hack-testing" every machine here and referring any
vulnerabilities found to the responsible person. They found an old
version of WU-FTP, one that I know can be over-flowed and subverted, on
one of "my" boxes. Someone else actually manages that machine, so I was
glad that my net-bosses told me of his sin. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 25 16:50:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Thu, 25 Oct 2001 17:50:59 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] gslgen & xitami & errors
References: <3BD82542.2090505@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <3BD834E3.9000305@freesbee.fr>

Francis Turner wrote:

> I started playing with gslgen to auto display some XML
>
> But there are times when I'd like to abort the file and return an 
> error. Is it possible to return HTTP error codes? And if so is it also 
> possible to redirect people using a 302 return?

Figured it out (partly) - redirects work by doing something like

.if %errorcondition%
  <HTML><HEAD><TITLE>XML Error</TITLE>
  <meta http-equiv="Refresh" content="0; 
URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower)/page.html"></HEAD>
  <BODY></BODY></HTML>
.  abort
.endif

 if  you replace the redirect 'URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower)/page.html' 
with 'URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower)/error?321' you get a error 321 page

 if you want a meaningful 404 error you do 
'URL=http://$(HTTP_HOST:lower)/$(PATH_INFO:lower)/error' which a) logs 
the error in a form that allows you to track it in the xitami log and b) 
gives the user something meaningful to note down when he complains

Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 25 18:48:08 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Thu, 25 Oct 2001 18:48:08 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] basic questions
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Thu, 25 Oct 2001 10:03:11 PDT."
 <5.0.2.1.0.20011025095950.020f3b70@mail.earthlink.net>
References: <5.0.2.1.0.20011025095950.020f3b70@mail.earthlink.net>
Message-ID: <E15wobw-0001Ow-00@entropy.ucam.org>

I'm not sure exactly what you're trying to achieve here. I'll assume you 
want to run Xitami on a reasonably workstation-type computer rather than a 
dedicated server.

First, try using Xitami with a web browser running on the same computer as 
Xitami itself, while claiming your IP address is "127.0.0.1". This is a 
reserved IP - *any* computer told to connect to 127.0.0.1 will connect to 
itself. http://127.0.0.1/admin should get you into the admin screen without 
even being connected to the Internet (note: you may need to turn off 
auto-dialling if you're using Internet Explorer and a dialup modem; my 
apologies if this sounds stupid, but I'm in the UK so I have no idea 
whether Earthlink is a dialup provider or cable or DSL or what).

Once it works with 127.0.0.1, try your dynamic IP (as reported by 
winipcfg). Unfortunately, your hostname will change with your IP (on many 
dynamic IP systems your hostname is something like 
modem-143.server-3.dialup.obscure.net) so giving your address to your 
friends could be tricky unless you use a dynamic DNS system (the Xitami 
docs include links to dyndns.org and others).

As for your domain, I can't tell how it's set up - is sound-computing.com a 
spare server box you own, or hosted on someone else's web server, or your 
workstation, or what? If that's not the machine you're trying to run Xitami 
on (which I assume it isn't since it's already running some other web 
server), it's irrelevant. For example, I have a domain which points to a 
commercial web host's Linux box (running Apache and various other servers), 
but that's completely irrelevant when I'm setting up Xitami on my own 
computer (whose domain is usually something horrible like 
modem-143.server-3.dialup.obscure.net).


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 25 19:09:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Thu, 25 Oct 2001 20:09:59 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] basic questions
References: <5.0.2.1.0.20011025095950.020f3b70@mail.earthlink.net>
Message-ID: <3BD85577.5040304@freesbee.fr>

dean martineau wrote:

> I'm trying to get started using the free version, and am finding the 
> documentation assumes I know much more than I do.  To begin with, I'm 
> trying to get into the configuration page.  As instructed in the .aug 
> file, I've tried to supply a username and password, but can't even 
> figure out where to put them.  the password seems easy to provide, but 
> not the username, and all combinations I try result in logon failure.


It may be disabled by default. Here is a fairly simple set of stuff to 
do (this assumes you have a clean Xitami config - ie. no changes to 
anything after the initial installation). It is possible that some or 
all of these steps will be performed during the installation so this is 
partly a check to make sure it is working right.

step 1.
Create (or edit ) a file called defaults.cfg in the xitami directory 
(usually c:\xitami\ for windows) and add a section as below:

[Security]
    Filename = "defaults.aut"

Save this file

step 2.
Create (or edit ) a file called defaults.aut in the xitami directory 
(usually c:\xitami\ for windows) and add a section as below:

[/admin]
    SecureName = "SecurePassword"

(obviously pick a different name/password combination to the above 
unless you want us to hack in!)
Save this file

step 3.
Check that Xitami is running (you have a green X icon in the system 
tray). It may already be running, if so thats fine if not run Xitami. If 
you don't get a green little icon then theres a problem right there. 
Possible errors (resulting in a red icon) are that you accidentally have 
another web server running

step 4
Start up your web browser and point it to http://localhost/ or 
http://127.0.0.1
You should get a Welcome to Xitami  screen

Somehwere on the left hand side you will see some text that say
'To configure the server, use the web-based admin 
<http://localhost/admin> function. This is password-protected.'
click on the link and enter the secureUser and securePassword you put in 
defualts.aut above
you should now be in the first admin screen- Click configuration to 
start configuring things

If you get to the first screen but all clicks just return you to it the 
most likely thing is that you are running a Netscape 6.x / Mozilla 
browser which objects to some Javascript that Xitami uses. Use a 
different browser would be my suggestion.

Francis

  experience is what you get when you don't." Pete Seeger

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Oct 25 23:32:37 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Thu, 25 Oct 2001 23:32:37 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] basic questions
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Thu, 25 Oct 2001 14:28:28 PDT."
 <5.0.2.1.0.20011025141743.02176840@mail.earthlink.net>
References: <5.0.2.1.0.20011025095950.020f3b70@mail.earthlink.net>
 <5.0.2.1.0.20011025141743.02176840@mail.earthlink.net>
Message-ID: <E15wt3F-0001eG-00@entropy.ucam.org>

In defaults.aut, the word before the = is your username, and the word after 
the = is your password. For example, this will let you log in to 
http://127.0.0.1/admin as a user "eviloverlord" with password "topsecret":

[/Admin]
    eviloverlord=topsecret

If you have admin=xxx and SecureName=xxx lines, you can log in as either of 
the users "admin" or "SecureName", with password "xxx" in either case. I 
assume you don't want this.

The one exception to this is "webmask=something", which sets which 
computers can access the admin screen (webmask=local will restrict it to 
the computer the server is actually running on).

If you're using Netscape 6 or Mozilla, you may need to edit defaults.cfg 
and add this:

[Console]
    Javascript = "0"

(if the [Console] section is already there, either add the Javascript key 
or edit it to switch it to 0). I couldn't use the Javascript admin 
interface with Mozilla 0.94, but it works now (in Mozilla 0.95), so your 
mileage may vary. I actually considered sending iMatix a patch to use 
different Javascript function names to avoid this problem, but the names 
are hard-coded into their form generating tool :-(
I might still try adapting it so the Javascript isn't critical: if I do, 
I'll definitely let iMatix know so they can merge it into some future 
version.

If you have a really screwed config, adding this to defaults.cfg may help:

[Wsx]
    admin=xiadmin

although this shouldn't be necessary.

The Xitami server itself is running under the NT Administrator user, so

permissions to all files on the local machine. The working dir. is set to
"-" as recommended, yet it manages to create temporary files in D:\Temp,

files?
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Sample Script:

#!perl

# Define Variables
	$Script;
	$lines;

# Read Name of Script
	$Script = $ENV{'SCRIPT_NAME'};
	if ($Script eq "") {$Script = "default.txt"};

# Open Script
	open(TXT, "<".$Script);
	@text=<TXT>;
	close(TXT);

# Print Script to screen
	&Header;
	print "\nScript to be processed: <b>".$Script."</b><hr>";
	foreach $line(@text){
		print "$line.<br>";
		$lines++;
	}
	if($lines<1){$lines="no"};
	&Footer;

sub Header{
	print "content-type:text/html\n\n<html>";
	print "<title>View File Script</title>";
}

sub Footer{
	print "There are <b>".$lines."</b> lines<br>";
	print "<b>The End</b>";
	print "</html>";
}
#	End viewfile.pl

To be a real CGI script (i.e. one that will work) I believe that's

---- begin
#!/usr/bin/perl

# for Windows + ActivePerl the above should work anyway;
# if not, use #!c:/perl/bin/perl or whatever

print "Content-Type:text/plain\n\n";
print "Hello, World!\n";
---- end

since you need at least a Content-Type header and a blank line (so two 
consecutive newlines) before the content starts.

> >  Perl script in webroot/cgi-bin
> 
> Ugh, that's asking for trouble. Better to be in /Xitami/cgi-bin, OUTSIDE
> the webpages folder, so nobody can read it. 

Indeed, is that the problem? /cgi-bin is (by default) an alias for 
c:\xitami\cgi-bin, which makes c:\xitami\webroot\cgi-bin "invisible" to the 
server...

>From what has been said on this board before, Xitami should work fine on XP.

If you are an avid Front Page user, then I am not sure that you will be
happy with Xitami.  Xitami is great, but it does not work with the Front
Page features:

1.) It does not support FP extensions such as THEMES.

2.) It can not update the site using the FP usual site update features since
Xitami will not open the site as an HTTP request.  You will have to publish
it locally, and then copy it over manually.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Oct 29 08:46:53 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Simon McVittie)
Date: Mon, 29 Oct 2001 08:46:53 +0000
Subject: [Xitami] restricting access
In-Reply-To: Your message of "Mon, 29 Oct 2001 05:38:48 GMT."
 <F89qf69aZbLAX3cf3ed00009040@hotmail.com>
References: <F89qf69aZbLAX3cf3ed00009040@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <E15y84L-0000G0-00@entropy.ucam.org>

[Security]
    webmask=!123.45.67.89,*

will deny requests from the IP 123.45.67.89 then allow from everyone else. 
See <your Xitami docs>/index4.htm#webmask (usually accessible as 
http://127.0.0.1/xitami/index4.htm#webmask while Xitami is running) for 
more details.

Note that, for real security, it may be better to IPban people using a 
firewall (if you do that, anyone connecting to your server from a banned IP 
will usually get no indication that a server even exists at your IP - they 
won't get an error from Xitami, but their computer will generate an error 
when its request times out). If you're doing this to prevent Code Red or 
other virus traffic, this is probably A Good Thing (the more time the virus 
spends waiting for a response which isn't going to arrive, the less time it 
has to flood you or other servers with requests).

Also note that the banned computer will be able to access your server 
through a proxy like their ISP's web proxy or the Google cache or whatever. 
If you're banning a human, this is an issue - if you're banning a 
virus-infected host, this shouldn't be a problem.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Oct 31 19:34:37 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (rob tromp)
Date: Wed, 31 Oct 2001 20:34:37 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Upload scripts on Xitami
In-Reply-To: <20011031173156.43919.qmail@web20007.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <NEBBJEPFPIGHFPCNGBGCCELICCAA.tromp@tromp.cx>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0008_01C1624B.75529460
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

Yes....

Her it is, it is rather basic, but it will work. You can modify and give it
a cosmetic facelift.
After sending the file, the file is diplayed. If you don't want this to
happen, modify the .class

Regards,
Rob


<html>
	<head>
		<title>Upload</title>
	</head>
<body>

<?
require("fileupload.class");

#--------------------------------#
# Variables
#--------------------------------#

// The path to the directory where you want the
// uploaded files to be saved. This MUST end with a
// trailing slash unless you use $PATH = ""; to
// upload to the current directory. Whatever directory
// you choose, please chmod 777 that directory.

	$PATH = "./images/";

// The name of the file field in your form.

	$FILENAME = "userfile";

// ACCEPT mode - if you only want to accept
// a certain type of file.
// possible file types that PHP recognizes includes:
//
// OPTIONS INCLUDE:
//  text/plain
//  image/gif
//  image/jpeg
//  image/png

	$ACCEPT = "";

// If no extension is supplied, and the browser or PHP
// can not figure out what type of file it is, you can
// add a default extension - like ".jpg" or ".txt"

	$EXTENSION = "";

// SAVE_MODE: if your are attempting to upload
// a file with the same name as another file in the
// $PATH directory
//
// OPTIONS:
//   1 = overwrite mode
//   2 = create new with incremental extention
//   3= do nothing if exists, highest protection

	$SAVE_MODE = 1;


#--------------------------------#
# PHP
#--------------------------------#

function print_file($file, $type, $mode) {
	if($file) {
		if(ereg("image", $type)) {
			echo "<img src=\"" . $file . "\" border=\"0\" alt=\"\">";
		}
		else {
			$userfile = fopen($file, "r");
			while(!feof($userfile)) {
				$line = fgets($userfile, 255);
				switch($mode){
					case 1:
						echo $line;
						break;
					case 2:
						echo nl2br(ereg_replace("\t",
"&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;", htmlentities($line)));
						break;
				}
			}
		}
	}
}

$upload = new uploader;
$upload->max_filesize(500000);

if($upload->upload("$FILENAME", "$ACCEPT", "$EXTENSION")) {
	while(list($key, $var) = each($upload->file)){
		echo $key . " = " . $var . "<br>";
	}
	if($upload->save_file("$PATH", $SAVE_MODE)) {
		print("<p>Saved as: " . $upload->new_file . "<p>");
		print_file($upload->new_file, $upload->file["type"], 2);
	}
}

if($upload->errors) {
	while(list($key, $var) = each($upload->errors)){
		echo "<p>" . $var . "<br>";
	}
}

if ($NEW_NAME) {
	print("<p>Name of sent file: <b>$NEW_NAME</b></p>");
}

#--------------------------------#
# HTML FORM
#--------------------------------#
?>

	<form enctype="multipart/form-data" action="<?print($PHP_SELF);?>"
method="POST">
		<input type="hidden" name="MAX_FILE_SIZE" value="100000">Send this file:
		<input name="userfile" type="file">
		<input type="submit" value="SEND">
	</form>
	<hr>
	[ <a href="../index.html">Home</a> ]
<?
	if ($ACCEPT) {
		print(" [ This form only accepts <b>" . $ACCEPT . "</b> files ] \n");
	}
?>

</body>
</html>

Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="fileupload.class"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable
Content-Disposition: attachment;
	filename="fileupload.class"

<?
/*
Error codes:
	0 - "No file was uploaded"
	1 - "Maximum file size exceeded"
	2 - "Maximum image size exceeded"
	3 - "Only specified file type may be uploaded"
	4 - "File already exists" (save only)
*/

class uploader {

	var $file;
	var $errors;
	var $accepted;
	var $new_file;
	var $max_filesize;
	var $max_image_width;
	var $max_image_height;

	function max_filesize($size){
		$this->max_filesize =3D $size;
	}

	function max_image_size($width, $height){
		$this->max_image_width =3D $width;
		$this->max_image_height =3D $height;
	}

	function upload($filename, $accept_type, $extention) {
		// get all the properties of the file
		$index =3D array("file", "name", "size", "type");
		for($i =3D 0; $i < 4; $i++) {
			$file_var =3D '$' . $filename . (($index[$i] !=3D "file") ? "_" . =
$index[$i] : "");
			eval('global ' . $file_var . ';');
			eval('$this->file[$index[$i]] =3D ' . $file_var . ';');
		}
=09
		if($this->file["file"] && $this->file["file"] !=3D "none") {
			//test max size
			if($this->max_filesize && $this->file["size"] > $this->max_filesize) =
{
				$this->errors[1] =3D "Maximum file size exceeded. File may be no =
larger than " . $this->max_filesize/1000 . "KB.";
				return False;
			}
	 		if(ereg("image", $this->file["type"])) {
	 			$image =3D getimagesize($this->file["file"]);
	 			$this->file["width"] =3D $image[0];
	 			$this->file["height"] =3D $image[1];
		=09
				// test max image size
				if(($this->max_image_width || $this->max_image_height) && =
(($this->file["width"] > $this->max_image_width) || =
($this->file["height"] > $this->max_image_height))) {
					$this->errors[2] =3D "Maximum image size exceeded. Image may be no =
more than " . $this->max_image_width . " x " . $this->max_image_height . =
" pixels";
					return False;
				}=09
	 			switch($image[2]) {
	 				case 1:
	 					$this->file["extention"] =3D ".gif";
	 					break;
	 				case 2:
	 					$this->file["extention"] =3D ".jpg";
	 					break;
	 				case 3:
	 					$this->file["extention"] =3D ".png";
	 					break;
	 				default:
						$this->file["extention"] =3D $extention;
	 					break;
	 			}
			}
	 		else if(!ereg("(\.)([a-z0-9]{3,5})$", $this->file["name"]) && =
!$extention) {
				// add new mime types here
				switch($this->file["type"]) {
					case "text/plain":
						$this->file["extention"] =3D ".txt";
						break;
					default:
						break;
				}		=09
	 		}
			else {
				$this->file["extention"] =3D $extention;
			}
	=09
			// check to see if the file is of type specified
			if($accept_type) {
				if(ereg($accept_type, $this->file["type"])) { $this->accepted =3D =
True; }
				else { $this->errors[3] =3D "Only " . ereg_replace("\|", " or ", =
$accept_type) . " files may be uploaded"; }
			}
			else { $this->accepted =3D True; }
		}
		else { $this->errors[0] =3D "No file was uploaded"; }
		return $this->accepted;
	}

	function save_file($path, $mode){
		global $NEW_NAME;
	=09
		if($this->accepted) {
			// very strict naming of file.. only lowercase letters, numbers and =
underscores
			$new_name =3D ereg_replace("[^a-z0-9._]", "", ereg_replace(" ", "_", =
ereg_replace("%20", "_", strtolower($this->file["name"]))));

			// check for extention and remove
			if(ereg("(\.)([a-z0-9]{3,5})$", $new_name)) {
				$pos =3D strrpos($new_name, ".");
				if(!$this->file["extention"]) { $this->file["extention"] =3D =
substr($new_name, $pos, strlen($new_name)); }
				$new_name =3D substr($new_name, 0, $pos);
			=09
			}
			$this->new_file =3D $path . $new_name . $this->file["extention"];
			$NEW_NAME =3D $new_name . $this->file["extention"];
		=09
			switch($mode) {
				case 1: // overwrite mode
					$aok =3D copy($this->file["file"], $this->new_file);
					break;
				case 2: // create new with incremental extention
					while(file_exists($path . $new_name . $copy . =
$this->file["extention"])) {
						$copy =3D "_copy" . $n;
						$n++;
					}
					$this->new_file =3D $path . $new_name . $copy . =
$this->file["extention"];
					$aok =3D copy($this->file["file"], $this->new_file);
					break;
				case 3: // do nothing if exists, highest protection
					if(file_exists($this->new_file)){
						$this->errors[4] =3D "File &quot" . $this->new_file . "&quot =
already exists";
					}
					else {
						$aok =3D rename($this->file["file"], $this->new_file);
					}
					break;
				default:
					break;
			}
			if(!$aok) { unset($this->new_file); }
			return $aok;
		}
	}
}
?>
